newly enpryted at Paris. M.D.xxxiij.

MARTIVS
March betokens te. vi. years following. Arayeng the earth with pleasant
verdure. That season youth cares for nothing. And without thought does his
sport and pleasure.

JULIUS.
At.xl. year of aege or elies never.

Loy. was. bar. ber. to. Ny. coll.

Sunday.
I Am sunday honorable
The heed of all the weke days
That day all thing labourable.
Ought to rest. and give lawde and prays
To our creator. that always
Would have us rest after travail
Man. servant. and thy be he says
And the other to thyn avail.
Monday
Monday. men ought me for to call
In which. god works ought to begin
Heryng mass. te first deed of all
Intendyng to fle deedly syn
This worldly goods truly to win
with labor and true excercyse
For who of good works can not blyn
To reward. shall wyn paradyse.
Tuesday.
I tuesday. am so named of mars
Called of gods army potent.
I love never for to be scars
Of work. but always dilygent
Stryuyng against life indigent
Being in this world: and else where
To serve our lord. with good intent
As of duty. we are bound here.
wednesday*
wednesday. sothely is my name
Amyd the weke is my being
wherein all virtues does frame
By the means of good living
I do remember the heaven king
That was sold in my season.
I do work with true meaning
Him to serve. as it is reason.
Thursday.
I am the meryest of seven
Called thursday verily.
In my time the king of heaven
Made his sowper meryly
In form of breed gave his body
To his appostles. as is plain
And than washed their fete mekely
And went to olyuet mountain.
Fryd^^
Named I am devout friday
The which cares for no delight
But to mourn. fast. deal. and pray
I do set all my hole appetyte
To think on the Jews despyte
How they did Christ on the tree rend
And thynkyng how I may be quyte
At the dredefull judgment.
Saturday.
Saturday I am coming last
Trustyng on the time spent well
Having ever mind steadfast
On that lord that harowed hell
That he my sins will expel
At the instaunce of his mother
whose goodness does far excel
whom I serve above all other.

FOr to begin the manner of salutary of helthfull living: and to come to
perfectyon (how well I have more need to be instruct than for to teache other)
yet keep these small doctrynes here following to your powers. First rise up
at.vj. of the clock i^ the morning in all seasons. And in your rysyng do as
follows. Thank our lord of the rest that he gave you that night. Commend
you to god. to our blyssed lady saint mary. and to that saint which is feested
that day / and to all the saints of heaven. Secondly beseech god that he
preserve the that day / from deedly sin / and at all other times And pray him
that all the works that other does for you may be accept to the lawde of his
name / of his glorious mother / and of all the company of heaven. when ye have
arrayed you. say in your chamber or lodgyng. matyns. pryme. and hours if ye
may. Than go to the church or ye do any worldly works if ye have no nedeful
business And abide in the church the space of a low mass while. where ye
shall think and ta^ke god of his benefits. Think a while on the goodness of
god / on his dyuine might / and virtue. Think what gift he has given to you
to create you so nobly / as to his image and likeness. Think also what grace
he has done to you in the sacrament of baptysme clensyng your soul from
sin. Think how many times ye have offended him sith ye were crystened.
Think how mekely he has abyden your retournyng from sin. Think from how
many dangers he has preserved your body and soul. Think how ill ye have
bestowed the time that he had given you to do penance. Think how many times
he had forgyuen you i^ shrist. And how many times ye have fallen to sin
again. Think in what pain ye has been now and ever if god had taken you out
of this world when ye were i^ deedly sin. Think how derely he bought you
from the danger of the devil. suffryng contynuall pains in this world.
about the space of.xxxij. years. going barefote in cold and heat. suffryng
hongre. and thyrst and many shame full iniuryes and how derely he redeemed you.
gyuyng his precious body. his blood. and his soul. And at this point consydre
all the pains of his woeful passion. as god will give you grace. Think also
what pain his dear and glorious mother suffered all that while. Co^sydre his
sharp judgment at the hour of your death. And touching this death think
often thereon / and that ye can not escape it / nor knows when. nor how. in
what estate. nor what place. nor time day. nor hour. Think than what shall
become of the worldly goods that ye have gadred and spared with great labor.
And how loathe ye shall be to leave them / and all your friends and kynsfolke.
And that more is when your soul in great pain shall leave your body to rotte
in the earth. Consydre than what shall be come of your strength beauty / you
the health / and other welthes of the body. Think what the poor soul shall
do when it gooth alone without company where it was never. Think what it shall
do when it sees the horrible enmyes that would draw it to perdicyon if ye
deye in deedly sin. Think how woeful a journey it shall be when ye must
yield a general reckoning of all your works / words / and thoughts: without
excepcyon of any thing. Think how god shall give you grace. Think on the
horrible pains of hell / and on the cruel company of deuylles: where without
end ye shall never have releas / if ye deye in deedly sin. And think on the
inestimable joy of the saints in heaven / the which our lord has promised
you if ye live out of deedly sin / and love him above all thing. And have ye
a perfyte hope if ye live well ye shall come to that glory. Amen.

And if by any other reasonable business ye may not be so long in the church
/ at it is said here before yield tankes to god of his goodness. And think on
the resydew in your hows ones in the day or in the night if ye may.

When ye are come fro the church take heed to your houswolde or ocupacyon till
dinner time. And in so doing think sometime that the pain that ye suffer in
this world is nothing to the regard often infinyte glory that ye shall have if
ye take it mekely. Than take your refection or mele reasonably without excess
or over much for beryng of your meat. for there is as much danger in to
little as in to much. if ye fast ones in a weke it is enough beside / vygilles
and ymbre days out of lenten. And if ye think te fasting be not good nor
prouffytable do by counsel. Rest you after dinner an hour or half an hour as
ye think best / prayeng god that i^ that rest he will accept your health / to
the e^de that after it ye may serve him the more devoutly. The residew of the
day bestow in your business to the pleasure of god. As touching your service
say unto tiers before dinner: and make an end of all before souper. And when ye
may / say dyryge and comme^dacyons for all christen fowls / at the leest way
on the holy days. And if ye have leaser say them on other days at the leest
with three lessons. Shryue you every weke to your curate except ye have great
let. and beware ye pass not a fourte night except very great let. if ye
be of power refuse not your alms to the first poor body that axeth it of
you that day / if ye think it needful. Take pain to here and keep the word
of god. Confess you every day to god without fail / of such sins as ye
know that ye have done that day. Consydre often either by day or night when ye
do awake what our lord did at that hour the day of his blyssed passion / and
where he was at that hour.

Seek a good and faith full friend of good conuersacyon to whom ye may
dyscouer your mind secrets. Enquere and prove him well or ye trust in him.
And when ye have well ^^es him do all by his counsel. Say little. and follow
virtuous company Eschew the felawshyppe of them that ye would not be like.
After all work praise and tanke god / love him above all things / and serve
him and his glorious mother diligently. do to none other but that ye would were
done to you. love the wealth of an other as your own. And in going to your
bed have some good thought either of the passion of our lord / or of your
sins / or of the pains that souls have i^ purgatory / or some other good
spiritual thought. And than I hope your living shall be acceptable and
pleasyng to god.

(...) sancti euange^^ (...) Gloria tibi domine.
IN principio erat verbu^ et verbu^ erat apud deum et deus erat verbu^. Hoc
erat in principio apud deu^. Oi^a per ipsum facta sunt: et sine ipso factu^ est
nichil. Quoth factu^ est in ipso vita erat: et vita erat lux hominum. Et lux in
tenebris lucet / and tenebre eam non comprehenderunt. Fuit homo missus a deo:
cui nome^ erat johannes. Hic venit in testimonium: vt testimonium perhiberet de
lumine / vt omnes crederent per illum. Non erat ille lux: sed vt testimonium
perhiberet de lumine. Erat lux vera: que illuminat omne^ hominem venientem in
hunc mundum.

In mundo erat and mu^dus per ipsum factus est: et mundus eum non cognouit. In
propria venit: and sui eu^ non receperunt. Quot quot autem receperunt eum:
dedit eis potestatem filios dei fieri / his qui credunt in nomine eius. Quino^
ex sanguinibus / neque ex voluntate carnis / neque ex voluntate viri: sed ex
deo nati sunt. Et verbum caro factum est: et habitauit in nobis. Et vidimus
gloriam eius: gloriam quasi vnigeniti a patre. Plenum gratie et veritatis.

Deo gratias. Te inuocamus / te adoramus / te laudamus: o beata trinitas.

IN illo tempore. Missus est gabriel a^gelus a deo in ciuitatem galilee / cui

Aue gratia plena dominus tecum: benedicta tu in mulicribus. Que cum audisset

a^gelus ei. Netimeas maria: i^uen isti enim gratia^ apud deum. Ecce co^cipies
in vtero et paries filium: and vocabis nomen eius iesum. Hic erit magnus: and
filius altissinu vocabitur. Et dabit illi dn^s deus sede^ david patris eius: et
regnabit in domo jacob in eternum: et regni eius no^ erit finis. Dixit autem

obumbrabit tibi. Ideoque and quod nascetur ex te sanctum: vocabitur filius dei.
Et ecce elizabeth cognata tua: et ipsa concepit filium in senectute sua. Et hic

(...) Gloria tibi domine.
CVm natus esset jesus in bethlee^ jude in diebus herodis regis: ecce magi ab
orient venerunt hierosolymam: dicentes. Vbi est qui natus est rex iudeorum?
Vidimus enim stellam eius in orient: et venanus cum muneribus adorare eum.
Audiens autem herodes rex turbatus est: et omnis hierosolyma cu^ illo. Et
co^gregans omnes principes sacer dotum et scribas populi: sciscitabatur ab eis
vbi christus nasceretur. At illi dixeru^t ei. In bethleem jude. Sic enim
scriptu^ est per prophetam. Et tu bethleem terra judah: nequaquam minima es in
principibus judah. Ex te enim exiet dux qui regat populum meum israel. Tunc
herodes clam vocatis magis: diligenter didicit ab eis te^pus stelle que
apparuit eis. Et mitte^s eos in bethleem dixit. Ite et interrogate diligenter
de puero: et cum inueneritis renu^ciate michi: vt et ego venie^s adorem eum.
Qui cu^ audissent regem: abierunt. Et ecce stella quam videra^t in orient.
antecedebat eos: vsque du^ venie^s staret supra vbi erat puer. Videntes autem
stellam magi: gauisi su^t gaudio magno valde. Et intrantes domu^ inueneru^t
pueru^ cum maria matre eius: et procidentes adorauerunt eum. Et aper it is
thesauris suis obtulerunt ei munera: aurum. thus. et myrrham. Et responso
accepto in somnis ne redirent ad herodem: per aliam viam reuersi sunt in
regionem suam. Deo gratias.

Sequentia sancti euangelij secundum Marcum. vt Gloria tibi domine.
IN illo tempore. Recumbentibus vndecim discipulis apparuit illis jesus: and
exprobrauit incredulitatem illorum et duricia^ cordis: quia his qui viderant
eum resurrexisse / non crediderant. Et dixit eis. Euntes in mundu^ vniuersum
predicate eua^gelium omni creature. Qui crediderit et baptizatus fuerit /
saluus erit. Qui vero non crediderit: conde^nabitur. Signa autem eos qui
crediderint: hec sequentur. In nomine meo demonia eijcient linguis loquentur
nouis: serpents tollent. Et si mortiferum quid biberint: no^ eis nocebit.
Super egros manus impone^t et been habebunt. Et dominus quidem jesus postquam
locutus est eis: assumptus est in celum / et sedet a dextris dei. Illi, autem
profecti predicauerunt vbique: domino cooperante et sermone^ confirmante:
seque^tibus signis. Deo gratias.

that I may dye in this holy faith / and fynably may come to the glory eternal

INITIVM SALVTIS NOTITIA PECCATI

For this cruel sin Nathan the prophet
David reproved: and blamed gretely.
wherefore Dauyd with heaviness replete.
Tenderly weeping cried: Peccaui.


DOmine ne in furore tuo arguas me: neque in ira tua corripias me.

^uomam sagitte tue in^^xe sunt michi: et confirmasti super me manum tuam.

^o^ est sanitas i^ carne mea a facie ire tue: no^ est pax ossibus meis a facie
peccatorum meorum.

^uonia^ iniquitates me supergresse sunt caput meum: et sicut onus grave
grauate sunt super me.

^utruerunt et corrupt sunt cicatrices me: a facie infipientie me.

^iser factus sum et curuatus sum vsque in finem: tota die contristatus
ingrediebar.

^uoniam lumbi mei impleti sunt illusionibus: et non est sanitas in carne mea.

Afflictus sum et humiliatus sum nimis: rugiebam a gemitu cordis mei.

Dn^e ante te omne desiderium meum: and gemitus meus a te non est absconditus.

^or meum co^turbatum est dereliquit me virtus mea: et lumen oculorum meorum
and ipsum non est mecum.

Amici mei et proximi mei: aduersum me appropinquauerunt et steterunt.

Et qui iuxta me erant de long steteru^t: and vim faciebant quiquerebant
anima^ mea^.

Et qui inquireba^t mala michi locuti sunt vanitates: and dolos tota die
meditantur.

A go autem tanquam surdus no^ audiebam: et sicut mutus non aperiens os suum.

Et factus sum sicut homo non audiens: et non habens in ore suo redargutiones.

Quoniam in te domine speraui: tu exaudies me domine deus meus.

Quia dixi nequando supergaudeant michi inimici mei: et dum commouentur pedes
mei super me magna locuti sunt.

Quoniam ego in flagella paratus sum: et dolor meus in conspectu meo semper.

Quoniam iniquitatem meam annunciabo: et cogitabo pro peccato meo.

^nimici autem mei viuunt et confirmati sunt super me: and multiplicati sunt
qui oderunt me inique.

Qui retribuunt mala pro bonis detrahebant michi: qnonia^ sequebar bonitatem.

^e derelinquas me domine deus meus: ne discesseris a me.

Inte^de in adiutorium meum: domine deus salutis me.

Gloria patri et filio: et spiritui sancto.

Sicut erat in principio et nunc et semper et in secula seculorum amen.

^Onditor celi et terre rex regu^ and dominus dominatiu^: qui me de nichilo

domine Parce michi christ: quia ego pauper multum offendi in superbia / in
auaritia / in gula / in luxuria / in vana gloria / in odio / in accidia / in
adulterijs / in furto / in mendacio / in blasphemia in ioco / in risu / in vbis
ociosis / in auditu / in gustu / in tactu / cogitando loquendo / operando / et
in omnibus modis in quibus ego fragilis homo and peccator peccare potui. Mea
culpa: mea culpa: mea maxima culpa. Ideo deprecor tuam clementiam que de celo
pro mea salute descendit: que david a peccati lavsu erexit. Parce michi domine:
parce michi christ: qui petro te neganti pepercisti. Tu es creator meus et
adiutor meus: plasmator meus et redemptor meus: gubernator meus et pater meus:
dominus meus et deus meus: et rex meus Tu es spes mea et fiducia mea:
gubernatio mea et auxiliatio mea: consolatio mea et fortitudo mea: defensio mea
et liberatio mea: vita mea: salus mea: et resurrectio mea. Tu es firmame^tum
meu^ et refugium meum: lumen meum et desiderium meum: adiutorium meum et
patrocinium meum. Te deprecor et rogo adiuua me et saluus ego: guberna me and
defend me: co^forta me et co^sola me: co^firma me and letifica me: illumina me
et visita me. Suscita me mortuu^ qr factura and opus tuu^ sum dn^e ne
despicias. Famulus and seruustuus sum quod uis indignus and peccator. Sz
qualiscu^que sim sieve bonus sieve malus: semper tuus su^. Ad que^ ergo fugiam:
nisi ad te vada^? Si tu me eijcis: quis me recipiet? Si tu me despicis: quis me
aspiciet? Et recognosce me indignu^ ad te refugie^tem quod uis sim vilis and
i^mu^dus: qr si vilis and i^mu^dus suz: potes me mu^dare. Si cecus sum potes me
illuminare. Si infirmus sum potes me sanare. Si mortuus et sepultus sum potes
me resuscitare: qr mayor est pietas tua quod impietas mea: plus potes dimittere
quod ego co^mittere: and plus parcere quod ego peccator peccare. No^ ergo
respicias domi^e neque atte^das multitudine^ iniquitatu^ mea rum: sed scdm
multitudine^ miserationum tuarum miserere mei: and propitius esto michi
miserrimo peccatori. Dic anime me: salus tua ego sum. Qui dixisti: nolo morte^
pcto^ris sed magis vt viuat and co^uertatur: convert me dn^e ad te et noli
irasci co^tra me. Deprecor te cleme^tissime pater propter misericordia^ tua^:

Salutatio ad beatam virgin^ (...)


AVe fuit prima salus
Qua vincitur hostis malus.
Remordet culpa noxia
Iuua nos. aue maria.
Maria dum salutaris
Ab angelo sic vocaris.
Nomen tuum demonia
Repellit. aue maria.
^ratia sancti spiritus
Fecundauit te penitus.
Gratiarum nunc premia
Da nobis. aue maria.
^lena tu es virtutibus
Pre cunctis celi ciuibus.
Virtutes et auxilia
Presta nunc. aue maria.
^ominus ab initio
Destinauit te filio.
Tu es matter et filia
Prefelix. aue maria.
^ecum letantur angeli
Et exultant archangeli.
Celi celorum curia
O dulcis. aue maria.
Benedicta semper eris
In terris et in superis.
Tibi nullus in gloria
Compar est. aue maria.
^u cum deo coronaris
Et veniam seruis paris.
Fac nobis detur venia
Precibus. aue maria.
In gentes mouent prelia
Mundus caro demonia
Sed defend nos o pia
O clemens. aue maria.
^ulieribus omnibus
Prelata summis opibus.
Reple nos tua gratia
Egentes. aue maria.
^t post partum velut prius
Virgo manens / et filius
Descendit sicut pluuia
In vellus. aue maria.
Benedictus sit filius
Adiutor et propitius.
Adiutrix et propitia
Sis nobis. aue maria.
^ructus tuus tam amauit

A devout prayer Jesus christ.
O My sovereign lord Ihesu the very sone of almighty god and of the most
clean and glorious vyrgin Mary / that suffered the bitter death formysake and all
mankind upon god friday and rose again the third day. I beseech the lord
have mercy upon me that am a wreched sinner but yet thy creature. And for thy
precious passion save me and keep me from all perils both bodyly and goostly
/ and specially from all things that might turn thy dyspleasure / and with
all my heart I tanke the most merciful lord for thy great mercyes that thou
have showed me in the great dangers that I have been in / as well in my soul
/ as in my body And that thy grace and endless mercy has ever kept me / spared
me and saved me frothe hour of my birth unto this time. I beseech the lord
that thy mercy may keep me for the all way / and I cry the mercy with all my
hole heart for my great offenses / for my great unkindness and for my wrethed
and sinful life / and that I can not led my life as thy servant I cry the
mercy.

Deus propitius esto michi peccatori vel peccatrici.

I thank the also with all my heart my most gracyous lord for the benefytes
and grace that thou have given me so largely in this world before many other
creatures which have a thousand times deserved better than I But most
gracious lord I confess and knowledge verily that all it comes of the werfore
with all my heart I tanke the. And all the worship the praysynge / and the
thank be to the and to none other.

^on nobis domine non nobis / sed nomini tuo da gloriam.

Here follows certaynes q^stio^s what is sin with the order of confession.
Hyrst. what is penitence? Penitence is the emendacyon of the life with in
ward contricyon of heart for the sin committed: with a full purpose never do
the sin again. What is the effect of penitence? Penitence makes aungelles
glad: iustyfyeth wicked persons: calls again the goodness lost: and draws
mankind unto everlasting life.

How many necessary things be long to penitence? Five which ben they. Hope of
forgyuenes: contricyon of heart: confession of the fault: fulfyllyng of such
things as the priest shall command and enjoin. and utterly to forsake
sin. How is sin avoided? By avoiding occasyon thereof: as is pleasusure:
the beholdynge of the wanton plays: evil company: and such other.

Who shall never be forgyuen? He that forgyueth not to other and he that to
his power will not restore again things wrongfully taken. How prouest thou
that? For it is said in the Pater nr^. Dimitte nobis debita nostra: sicut et
nos dimittimus debiroribus nr^is. Good lord for give us as we forgive. And
saint Augustine says. No^ dimittitur pctm^ nisi restituatur ablatu^. The sin
is never forgyuen till the thing wrong fully taken be restored. Therefore wha^
we offend in word / or indede we ought to our power make satisfaccyon. And
what evil will / malice / or hatred we have conceived against any we should
put it out of our mind / to the end that our confession may be acceptable to
god. What is co^fessyon? Confession is the declaracyon of sin before a pressed
/ or any other in necessite. Under what manner ought the confession be? True of
thy propre sins hole / spedefull of the sure manerly / voluntarely clear with
such delyberacyon that it may plainly be understand: and wit so great
contricyon that it may make the sorry and heavy to have committed those sins /
fully minding never to return to them again: and so for the surely
purposynge to do penance.

What should I do willing to be confessed? Before all things i^ thy bed /
chamber? or other secret place much and often times think by thy self /
where / how when with whom / how many times / and how enormely thou have
sinned / wether i^ speaking / conse^te / will / or deed / what good deed thou
haste left which thou ought to have done. Nor it is not sufficyent to
confess the a liar: but thou must hole express what ill has followed upon
that lie. Nor thou shall not only say. I have sinned in glotony but thou must
tell how much whether thou were dronken / or dydest vomyte. ^c. in what place
it was / and how often. And when thou diligently by thy selphe have discussed and
considered all things / than go thou to the priest with great reverence / and
not as thou would tell a a tale: and after the sign of the cross made upon
thy breast say. Benedicite. Than after a few words spoken of the priest / thou
shall proceed in this manner. Confiteor deo celi. etc. till thou come to mea
culpa.

Than begin to declare how thou have sinned. First in thought / after in
speaking: lastely in warke and omyssyon. In warke in the seven deedly sins in
the sins against the holy ghost. etc. Omyssyon in the commandments and
warkes of mercy. etc. what is sin? There are two latin words for sin / one
called pctm^ the other delictu^. Pctm^ is the synwhan we be dysobedie^t to te
commandments of god. Delictu^ is the sin when we leave a good work undone
/ the which we ought to have done / but the difference of these two latin
words are almoost co^funded. How many manner of sins are there? Three.
Original sin of our holy fader Ada^ wiche is put away by baptym. Venial /
ready always to be forgyden / also without co^fessyon. Mortal sin which
without co^fessyon and penance leueth man to everlasting death. How many
mortal sins ben there? Seven. pride / wrath / envy glotony / lechery
slouthe and couetyse. Which be the sins against the holy ghost? Pertiuacite
/ stryuynge against the trinyte: by cause god is mercy full to sinners: despere
of the forgyuenes of god: obstinatio^ in evil hatred and envy of thy
neighbors virtue: ewident despysynge of penance. Which be sins causyng
euylles for to be done? Irritacyon / consent / co^sell / laudacyon / permission
/ socoure / and also participacyon. which be the sins cryenge before god for
vengeance? Manslaughter / sin against nature / oppression of poor people /
and with holding of dettes. which ben the circu^staunces augme^tynge sin?
Order: time: science: aege: condicyon: no^bre: abiding: abondaunce: cause:
manner: dignyte: and weyke resistance. etc. And than begin your confession
after in this manner.

The form of confession.
First I knowledge my self gylty unto almighty god unto our lady saint Mary:
and to all the company of heaven and to you my goostly fader: that sith ^ the
time of my last confession I have offended my lord god grievously / and
specially in the seven deedly sins.

Pride.
I Have sinned in pride of heart / not lowly thanking god of gifts and
conning which he has sent me. Also I have sinned i^ pride of clothing: in
strength: in eloquence: in beauty: in proud words. whereof I cry god mercy.

En^^
Also I have sinned in envy herynge any man more praised tha^ I or better
cherysshed with his sovereign than I / or he has more prosperity than I and
wha^ I have my sauswered mine even christian reioysynge. whereof I cry god mercy.

(...)
Also I have sinned in wrath: as in rygour of heart against mine even christian
whether it were little matter or great and for every word I wylled to be
avenged on them and answered them with evil words: and of smytyng them.
whereof I cry god mercy.

Sloute.
Also I have sinned in slouthe: and specially in geuynes of heart: and delyted
me in ylde thoughts and ymaginacyons of the world and my flesh / not
thanking god of his benefyte neither being sorry for my sins nor occupied
myself in good prayers nor holy meditacyons for the conforte of my soul.
whereof I cry god mercy.

Couetyse.
Also I have sinned in couetyse by unlawful desires of worldly goods in
misspendynge and unreasonably keeping of them: and I have / ouermoche desired
welt and prosperity and more worldly worship and richesse than I had / and
grutched at tribulacyons / aduersyte and pouerte whereof I cry god mercy.

Glotony.
Also I have sinned in glotony by unreasonable lusts of metes and drynkes /
more for flesshely lust tha^ for bodyly sustenaunce / and I have that great
excess of metes and drynkes so that nature might not ber it whereby I was the
worse disposed to serve my lord god and the more styred to sin / wrath / and
wrethchednes. whereof I cry god mercy.

Lechery.
Also I have sinned in lechery / by foul touching by thought of fylthy lusts
and uncleanness / sometime in deed done / in pollucyons and feeling of mine own
flesh / also in sight of virgyns and wydowes whereof I cry god mercy.

The.x. commaund^mentes.
Also I have sinned in brekyng of the x. commandments. I have not loved my
lord god above all thing / nor my neighbors al my self. I have customably
sworn by my lord god / by his name in vain / by his sweet body and his
saints all. I have not hallowed the feestes and holy days commannded by the
church. I have not done dew reverence to my fader and mother nor to my goostly
fades / nor followed their techynge. I have sinned in backbitynge mine even
christ in depravynge of their good name (...) and defylynge them with my
words. I have harmed my neighbors taking the yr goods against their will by
wrong. I have sinned flesshely with persons that been wedded and other moo /
and more would if I might have had time and place.

I have borne falls wytnes against mine even christian. I have coueyted to have my
neighbors wife / daughter or servant / and would if I had might. I have
inordinatly, coueyted the goods of my neighbors contrary to the laws of god.
whereof I cry god mercy.

The.v. wits.
I Ferthermore I have sinned in mysspe^dyng of my.v. wits / that is to say /
in sight of eyes / tastynge of mouth / herynge of here is / smelling of nose:
touching of hands and fete and with other members if the body. whereof I cry
god mercy.

The.vij. works of mercy bodyly.
Also I have sinned in not fulfyllynge of the.vij. works of mercy bodyly: by
will: power and deed. I have not clothed the naked. I have not given drink to
the thyrsty. I have not fed the hungry. I have not visited the prisoners and
the seek I have not departed of my goods to the poor I have not harbored the
harborlesse. I have not buried the deed according to the commandments of
god. whereof I cry god mercy.

The.vij. works of mercy goostly.
Also I have sinned in not fulfyllynge the.vij. works of mercy spyrytuall. I
have not given counseyll to them that had need. I have not taught the ignorant.

I have not discretly corrected them that have offended. I have not conforted
them that have been in heaviness. I have not forgyuen them that have mysdone or
myssayd by me. I have not patiently suffered them that have reproved me. I have
not devoutly prayed to god for my neighbor to give him grace to amend his
synful living and continue in virtue.

The.vij. gifts of the holy ghost.
Also I have not used the gifts of the holy ghost to the honor of god: as the
gift of understanding: the gift of wisdom: the gift of counseyll: the
gift: of science: the gift of strength: the gift of pity: and the gift of
dread. whereof I cry god mercy.

The.vij. sacraments.
Also I have not given tankes to our lord forte.vij. sacraments. As the
sacrament of baptym: of confirmation: of penance: of the body: of our lord:
of wedlock: of priest hode: and of enelynge. whereof being repentaunt. I cry
god mercy.

The.viij. beatitudes
Also I have not disposed me to the.viij. beatitudes: as pouerte of spirit /
perfyte mekenes in aduersite / perfyte mekenes in prosperyte / lust of right
wylnesse / perfyte mercy / clennesse of heart: peace in desire. Joyful suffrance
of persecucyon in the cause of virtue. whereof I cry god mercy.

Of these and all other: known and not known that ever I did sith I was
borne unto this day I ask god mercy: and most mercy full lord god. I yield
me gylty unto the and utterly put me unto thy grace: pity and mercy: and I
pray you my goostly fader to be between my sin and me that god of his mercy
forgive me for this lowly co^fessyon that I may be free fro my goostly ennemy
and optayn the endless bliss that god has bought me to. Ideo deprecor. (...).
